[THOUGHT: True]
The drone is currently at (6.43, 6.94) with 92% battery. A recent thermal scan at 225 degrees revealed a strong heat signature with a 52% signal strength at a bearing of 230.2 degrees and a distance of 3.81 units. This indicates a high probability of a survivor and takes precedence over general sector exploration. I will prioritize moving towards this strong signal.

First, I need to calculate the precise coordinates of this strong heat signature.
Current position (x, y) = (6.43, 6.94)
Distance = 3.81
Bearing = 230.2 degrees

Using trigonometry:
Target X = Current X + Distance * sin(Bearing in radians)
Target Y = Current Y + Distance * cos(Bearing in radians)

Bearing in radians = 230.2 * (pi / 180) = 4.0177 radians

Target X = 6.43 + 3.81 * sin(4.0177) = 6.43 + 3.81 * (-0.640) = 6.43 - 2.4384 = 3.9916
Target Y = 6.94 + 3.81 * cos(4.0177) = 6.94 + 3.81 * (-0.768) = 6.94 - 2.92768 = 4.01232

So, the target coordinates for the strong signal are approximately (3.99, 4.01).

A strong heat signature with 67% signal strength has been detected at a bearing of 233.9 degrees and a distance of 2.83 units. This is a very high probability of a survivor. I will now calculate the precise coordinates of this new, stronger heat signature.

Current position (x, y) = (5.79, 6.17)
Distance = 2.83
Bearing = 233.9 degrees

Using trigonometry:
Bearing in radians = 233.9 * (pi / 180) = 4.0823 radians

Target X = Current X + Distance * sin(Bearing in radians)
Target Y = Current Y + Distance * cos(Bearing in radians)

Target X = 5.79 + 2.83 * sin(4.0823) = 5.79 + 2.83 * (-0.708) = 5.79 - 2.00364 = 3.78636
Target Y = 6.17 + 2.83 * cos(4.0823) = 6.17 + 2.83 * (-0.706) = 6.17 - 1.99898 = 4.17102

So, the new target coordinates for the strong signal are approximately (3.79, 4.17).

Before committing to this move, I must verify if the drone has enough battery to reach these new target coordinates and return safely to base.

Alright, coordinates time: Target X = Current X + Distance * sin(Bearing in radians). Target Y = Current Y + Distance * cos(Bearing in radians).

So, the target's X coordinate is 3.18 + 2.98 * sin(6.0545), which works out to 3.18 + 2.98 * (-0.226). That simplifies to 3.18 - 0.67348, giving us 2.50652.

The Y coordinate should be 4.6 + 2.98 * cos(6.0545), which yields 4.6.

Therefore, the target coordinates are approximately (2.50652, 4.6). Now we have the location and can begin a more detailed analysis to determine the best course of action.

Current position (x, y) = (2.8, 8.52)
Distance = 3.99
Bearing = 355.7 degrees

First I need to convert the bearing from degrees to radians, I can use the formula, radians = degrees * (pi/180). This comes out to 6.208 radians.

Next, I can plug in the knowns into the formulas.
Target X = Current X + Distance * sin(Bearing in radians)
Target Y = Current Y + Distance * cos(Bearing in radians)

Target X = 2.8 + 3.99 * sin(6.208) = 2.8 + 3.99 * (-0.075) = 2.8 - 0.29925 = 2.50075
Target Y = 8.52 + 3.99 * cos(6.208) = 8.52 + 3.99 * 0.997 = 8.52 + 3.978 = 12.498

So, the target coordinates are approximately (2.50075, 12.498). Now I need to plot that on the system and adjust the drone's course.
